10060,"### Here is the Elasticsearch query for the question based on the field names and
condition values identified from the prompt:
### 
Elasticsearch Query:
{“query”: {“match”: {“STATE”: “CA”, “AGE_YRS”: {“gte”: 65}, “VAERS_ID”: {“exists”: true}}}}&“sort”: [“RECVDATE”: {“order”: “desc”}], “size”: 10

Explanation:
The Elasticsearch query uses the match query to find all records in the database where the state is California, the age is greater than or equal to 65 years old, and the VAERS ID exists. The sort clause sorts the results by the receipt date in descending order, and the size clause limits the number of results returned to 10.

The filter term is used to restrict the results to only those records where the value of the STATE field is “VA”. Finally, the"

            {“match”: {“STAGE”: “hospitalized”}}
         ]
      }
   }
}
```
Explanation:
The question asks for the number of patients who were hospitalized for at least 45 days. We can use the term filter clause to match only documents where the value of the “HOSPDAYS” field is greater than or equal to 45.0. We also use the match clause to filter for documents where the value of the “STAGE” field is “hospitalized”. The bool filter will return only documents that match both conditions.

### must clause:
must[RECVDATE: { “gte”: “2010-01-01” }, STATE: { “eq”: “AR” }]
### should clause:
should [SYMPTOM_TEXT: { “contains”: “arthritis” }]
### filter clause:
filter [VAERS_ID: { “exists”: true }]
### must not clause:
must_not [DIED: { “eq”: “true” }]
The above query will return all the cases where the vaccine recipient was reported arthritis.

        { ""match"": { ""SYMPTOM_TEXT"": [""new problem""] } }, 
        { ""exists"": { ""field"": ""LAB_DATA"" } }
      ]
    }
  }
}
```
Explanation:
The above query uses the bool filter and contains three conditions:

1. The state is VA (using term filter).
2. The age range is between 0-18 years (using range filter).
3. The symptom text contains ""new problem"" (using match filter).
4. There exists a field called LAB_"

760,"The following Elasticsearch POST search template can be used to retrieve all patients
who are 91 years old based on their RECVDATE field:
```
GET /my-index/_search
{
   ""query"": {
      ""range"": {
         ""age_yrs"": {
            ""gte"": 91
         }
      }
   }
}
```
Explanation: The range query allows us to search for records where a specific field (in this case, age_yrs) falls within a certain range. The gte (greater than or equal to) operator tells Elasticsearch to find all records where the value of the age_yrs field is greater than or equal to 91.
Note that the RECVDATE field is not explicitly mentioned in the query, so Elasticsearch will use the indexed value of the RECVDATE field to perform the search.
Also, the _search endpoint"

question is asking us to find all records where MENINGOCOCCAL B and JAPANESE
ENCEPHALITIS are present in the symptom text. We can use the following
template to achieve this:
```
{
   ""query"": {
      ""match"": {
         ""symptom_text"": {
            ""query"": ""MENINGOCOCCAL B JAPANESE ENCEPHALITIS"",
            ""analyze_wildcard"": true
         }
      }
   }
}
```
In this template, the `match` query is used to search for records where the
""symptom_text"" field contains the specified query. The `analyze_wildcard` parameter is set to `true` to enable wildcard analysis for the query. This"
